< text>
Super covid-19 conscientious!...which is fine. They have a step-by-step process in which they serve you. Once you enter...you sanitize at the station to the right. Then you proceed to the counter where you receive plastic gloves and your yogurt container. Customers are allowed to fill it themselves, however you must have the employee add the toppings. That is the one part I did not like. They decide how much of what. Personally, I like to fill yogurt half way, then sprinkle some toppings, and then get more yogurt. This way he don't reach the bottom and have no toppings. I understand the need for cleanliness to avoid germs and infection when serving food. It's a little bizarre that now all of a sudden people are very concerned about washing hands and cleaning services. Perhaps we should have been doing this all along! My only suggestion for you Yogurtland, maybe find another method other than the plastic gloves for every customer. It just seems so wasteful. I'm pretty sure that the sanitizing is enough at that point... Especially when it was not required in the first place.< /text>

<user_name>Kim Strange<//user_name><pics>None</pics>< Text>
Stayed 4 nights in March 2021.  It was my first time staying here.  Campground is on west side of the lake a little further away from highway 395 than the day use area.  Still heard some road noise from large trucks at night - but not too bad.  Also had some military jets flying low on 1 night that added noise.  Cell reception was great on Verizon LTE.  Never saw an attendant at the entrance station.  We did not have reservations - check in was via on-site pay station, rate was $14 a night.  Campground was clean.  Ample potable water spigots.  No fire wood for sale but there was ample wood on the ground.  Lone Pine is just a few miles up the road for gas and supplies.  Overall had a nice stay - gave 4 stars due to road noise.</Text>

<Pics>None< /Pics><review>My wife and I got engaged here and we love coming back and camping here. Only downfall this year is the well has been contaminated and they no longer have running water, so there is no showers on site. If you need to shower or plan on staying for a while make sure to find out where you can shower in town. Fishing during the summer is not all that good but picks up through the fall to spring. Weather is always nice and plenty of shade from the large trees around the lake. Make sure you bring trash bags to keep your camp clean and dispose of them in the dumpsters provided so that the park will stay clean.
The staff is very informative on the area and can give you information about whatever you may be looking for.<//review></record>

<time>1439572407253< /time><Rate>4<//Rate><Review>There is an amazing playground that is a perfect spot to stop and let kids play on long road trips. There was a restroom available near the park area too.

We stopped here with our RV for the night and it was a perfect rest stop for us. We paid $14 at an automated kiosk and visited with a really nice man that worked in the little office before selecting our lake-side camp site.  As many reviewers have said, it's a bit older facility but it was perfect for us since our RV is fully self contained.
It's a busy place at night with cars and RV's pulling in after midnight. There are  A LOT of bugs too, not the kind that bite you...just bug you. We're not really bothered by bugs so it wasn't a big deal for us.
Stargazing is amazing here. We were lucky enough to stop during a meteor shower and it was breathtaking.<//Review>< pictures>

< user_name>
Kristin Conover< /user_name>
< time>
1493081437702< /time>
< Rating>
3<//Rating>
<Text>The scenery is beautfiul, the fish were plentiful and my family had a great time for the two nights we stayed there but there were a few very important issues that made me give this campground a 3 rating.

1. I've read reviews that mentioned flush toilets. There are no flush toilets on site. For over 100 numbered sites, they had one building with two pit toilets (tent camping had another building). It was a slow weekend and it was still not stocked with enough toilet paper. They did have one Porta potty, but it was there from Sat - Mon without being emptied, no toilet paper, and just gross even for a Porta potty.
2. We had a great numbered spot (66) with great views and access to fishing right outside our tent and a table with a cover and BBQ pit right next to us, but the site was littered with trash and cigarette butts. It also looked as though the firepit had been moved to 4 different spots and we had a hard time finding a place for our tent in an otherwise very spacious spot. It was also quite a distance to the only bathroom for the numbered sites.
3. Highway noise. Camping is as far from the highway as you can get and still be next to the lake, and it's not an overwhelming sound. Most nights the frogs, birds and fish splashing near the shore made more noise the cars, but if being out in the middle of nowhere is what you're going for, this isn't the campground for you.

We got asked quite a few times by people who were trying to get a spot about checking in. If you didn't reserve your spot through Reserve America, there is a Kiosk in the day area (next to a map of the lake) to check in.

No hookups. Primitive spots. No showers. We did have a water spicket near our site, but it didn't look like there was a lot of sources for water and we dont know if it was potable water.

We went during off season and it wasn't very busy. I can this place being overwhelmingly busy during the summer. Even on a slow weekend, we had lots of traffic though the campground even at night.<//Text>< Pictures>
None</Pictures>

< review>
Good experience at Salang Pass trying Afghan food for the first time. I had the qabili pallow, "Afghanistan's most famous dish". < GmapID>
0x808fbf9cc52a3b53:0x48cb990b854165d9< /GmapID>
</record>
</dataset><record>
<resp>None</resp>< Review>
First off, the food is tasty.  A Qaubili pilau with a grilled amb shank was delicious, and a chicken qorma was likewise.  That said, I'm pretty sure Gordon Ramsay would end up in jail after what he'd do if he were to see the kitchen in action on a Saturday night.  Per one of the waiters, much of the food is pre-cooked and reheated--and not just reheated, it's MICROWAVED.  Uncooked meat (lamb shanks, particularly) is kept in bags on the floor, next to the garbage can.  We asked to be seated near the back so our 2-year-old wouldn't bother the other customers, but the owner (who acted as the host) was reluctant to do so; after seeing the kitchen, we understand why.  The basket of naan is hilariously underfilled--seriously, it's got about as much flour in it as four slices of Wonder Bread. The salads that come with the entrees are stingy, pathetically presented, and are tossed with what tastes an awful lot like Wishbone Italian dressing.

The decor is tacky and the place is starting to look a bit frayed about the edges.  The whole place is definitely on the unclean side and the women's restroom is appallingly dirty; it didn't even have soap.  The tables are sticky, and the waiters are scarce.

I've been to some excellent Afghan restaurants both here and in the DC/Northern Virginia area, where the service was superb and the food fresh.  This is not one of them.  Salang Pass is easily the worst Afghan restaurant I've ever visited, and I highly recommend that you avoid it.<//Review>

< review>
My gym closed it's doors so I really only had 2 other options in my area. It was Crunch or 24hr Fitness. I went with Crunch because I like to stay focused on my work out when I'm at the gym and don't like waiting in line for a machine to open up. Crunch is big enough that you don't feel like you're working out on top of each other. The staff is courteous and doesn't interfere with your routine. I  hate 24hr Fitness it's over crowded and people are too into how they look working out not how effective the work out actually is. Only 2 things I wish Crunch could fix is the funky smell from the A.C. and if they could get heavier dumbbells they only go as high as 80lbs.</review>

< text>
I was looking to get a new complete after leaving my board in storage at school.

I tried looking in my hometown, Oxnard, for some locally owned skate shops but they were all close down so I went over to Ventura to see if there were any good ones.

I can honestly recommend this skate shop to anyone, especially beginners. I was helped out by Frank who knew all his stuff with regards to boarding and his connection definitely highlighted it.

I went in looking for a classic board setup but left with a beautiful board. As we were selecting components Frank helped me choose between items with his experience and input--which are thoroughly appreciated.

He was also to give me history about the board and the area while he set it up for me. If you're looking for a locally owned shop with experienced and friendly employees, this is definitely the spot.<//text>

< Review>
I rarely write reviews, but I have to in this case. I called in asking about Sector 9 boards (that was the only manufacturer I knew at the time), and Dave said he'd be happy to show me a few. I went in to the store, and Dave let me check out some boards and knew the answers to every single question I had. None of the Sectors felt right, so he suggested I try a different manufacturer, based on what I said I wanted in a board, and he pulled on from the wall. It was EXACTLY what I was looking for. He then changed the wheels to the color I wanted, free of charge, gave me some insight on skateboard manufacturers and the sport, and sent me on my way. I've had my skateboard for a few weeks now, and I love it. If it weren't for Dave, I'd be riding a board that isn't quite what I wanted. Don't look any further than Five Points.<//Review>

<Review>I really wanted to give the folks at BoxDog a chance, as i had heard great things about their service department,. Unfortunately, the service i received was quite poor.

In March, I brought a brand new fork in to have BoxDog install it, cut the steerer, and install and bleed the hydraulic brake. The drop-off process was pretty straight forward. I brought the bike in mocked up as i wanted it, discussed it with the owner, and left. When i came back a few days later to pick it up, they had not followed my instructions, and they cut the fork too short for my needs. Frustrating, but understandable that there are sometimes communication issues between the person checking the bike in and the person performing the work. Problem was, the fork that i  had supplied was the last one available in the US for many weeks. After much communication with the owner, he agreed to replace the fork for me at no charge, as long as i paid for the labor when i picked it up. I paid $130 for the install and took my bike home for the long wait for the replacement fork.

At the end of May, i got an email from the owner saying that my fork had arrived and i should drop my bike off to have it installed. Again, easy drop off and no issues. Had a nice conversation with the owner when i dropped it off. He mentioned that he was glad that i had brought the bike back to them so that they could make it right, instead of just finding a new shop to work with. I asked if they would swap the front rack and wired headlight over to the new fork, and he said it would be no problem.

The next day, i got a call that my bike was ready and went to pick it up. When i got the bike, everything LOOKED correct. I was, however, shocked to find that the owner was charging me an additional $65 for the headlight installation, which was never mentioned to me at any point in time. I was not happy, but felt that i had to pay in order to get my bike back. The owner ‚Äúkindly‚Äù gave me a 50% discount on the additional labor that they were chiseling out of me.

I rode the bike across town and immediately put it in the stand to check the work. No offense to the shop, but i no longer trusted their work without checking it myself. I was quite disappointed to again find incredibly sloppy and unsafe work. The steerer was again cut shorter than i had requested.

Worst of all, every single rack mounting bolt was hand tight. If they had worked their way loose, i would be facing a serious accident, or possibly death.

I emailed the owner to let him know that i found the work shoddy, and that they had allowed a bike to leave the shop patently unsafe. I still have not received a response from the owner. In the end, BoxDog thinks that the sloppy work they performed is worth nearly $200. I‚Äôve included photos of both forks as i got them from the shop. I‚Äôve shared the photos with other bike shop employees, and to a one, they have said that it is poor work.

Their shop has a number of nice things to sell, but i would not recommend their service department. < text>
Box Dog Bikes is a gem in the heart of the city and right off the bike lane on 14th St! They're just a few blocks from the 16th St Bart station and right up the street from Dolores Park. I have been shopping at BDB since way back in 2013. I remember when the dog used to actually ride in the box ;)

This shop is truly a gem in this mega corporate bike shop world. They're a worker-owned cooperative and it shows by the work that each and every worker puts out. From Paul to Geoff to Angus to Emily to Sarah and Eric, (sorry I'm missing a few), these cats know bikes! They're selection is up to date with the coolest bikes in the industry and if that doesn't float yer boat take a look at their house designed, made in the USA, Pelican frame! This thing is a front loader (hence the name) and of course it's made of the finest of American steel. If you're looking for more than bikes, take a look at their USA made cycling bag selection; stocked with the coolest and and hottest names in the bike bag market. I've been working with Box Dog Bikes on a B2B level for the past few years and I couldn't be happier with their attention to detail as well as their communication skills from a business standpoint. Cheers to BDB and maybe we will catch ya for one of your overnighter rides soon!</text>

Where do I begin?  I'll walk through the entire experience.

A few months ago, I met Chris Chrostowski (Sales Consultant) when I was helping my friend purchase pre-owned vehicle from their lot.  After a great experience, I told Chris that when I was ready to buy a car, I'd return to his dealership and work with by name.  Before making my way to dealership, I decided to appraise my vehicle via the Nissan website (fairly straightforward, very easy to use).  Once done with that, I received an email from Zack Bilbrey, (Internet Sales Manager) informing me of some purchasing options, and assuring me that I would be able to work with Chris.  Once I get to the dealership, both Chris and Zack greet me and reassure that a favorable deal will get done.  Midway through the process, I am introduced to Nick Dubiel (General Sales Manager). In accordance with the others, Nick made sure that I was able to get a good deal with low interest and reasonable payments.  He was friendly, attentive, and was committed to go out of his way to accommodate.  Lastly there was Eric ZuWalick, the Finance Manager.  Probably the most reassuring things about Eric was the fact that he was clear in his communication with me and he made me completely aware of all extended protection options that were available to me.  He took his time explaining everything to me and answered all of my questions.

I understand this a bit of a lengthy read, but these 4 completely deserve it.  I expect this kind of service from an individual when I make significant purchases like this, but to see everyone try so hard for me and for them all to be on the same page like that is truly unique.  I felt like I've known them all for years.  With that said, whatever you guys are doing over at Mossy Nissan Escondido, keep it up!  I've been apart of a few car purchases, but none of them stack to up to this experience.
